       <script type="text/javascript">
        var Spotlight = {
    init: function () {
      $(".js-spotlight:visible").on("mouseover", "li:first", function () {
        $(this).addClass("focused");
      });
      $(".js-spotlight:visible").on("mouseout", "li:first", function () {
        $(this).removeClass("focused");
      });
      var ticker = function () {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var $spotlight = $('.js-spotlight:visible');
          if (!$spotlight.find('li:first').hasClass('focused')) {
            $spotlight.find('li:first').animate({
              marginTop: '-20px'
            }, 800, function () {
              $(this).detach().appendTo($spotlight).removeAttr('style');
            });
          }
          ticker();
        }, 4000);
      };
      ticker();
    }
  };
  $(document).ready(function () {
    Spotlight.init();
  });
       </script>

      <script>
       function getParameterByName(name, url) {
        if (!url) url = window.location.href;
        name = name.replace(/[\[\]]/g, "\\$&");
        var regex = new RegExp("[?&]" + name + "(=([^&#]*)|&|#|$)"),
          results = regex.exec(url);
        if (!results) return null;
        if (!results[2]) return '';
        return decodeURIComponent(results[2].replace(/\+/g, " "));
      }
      </script>

         <div class="section__header">
          <div class="h1 section__title">
           French legend eyes World Cup history with Guinea
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="fi-article-feature-bg__mask--nobrand">
         <div class="fi-module-player__bg">
          <picture>
           <!--[if IE 9]><video style="display: none;"><![endif]-->
           <source data-srcset="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_l1/v1615911178/y0bdbvti7q2mmdschjdr.jpg" media="(min-width: 1200px)"/>
           <source data-srcset="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_tc1/v1615911178/y0bdbvti7q2mmdschjdr.jpg" media="(min-width: 1024px)"/>

           <img alt="Didier Six module 2" class="img-responsive lazyload" data-src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_p3/v1615911178/y0bdbvti7q2mmdschjdr.jpg" onerror="setDefaultPicture(this,'t_l1', 't_tc1', 't_l3', 't_p3');" src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_tc1/t_lazy/v1615911178/y0bdbvti7q2mmdschjdr.jpg"/>

        <div class="container-fluid">
         <div class="row">
          <div class="col-sm-6 col-md-5">
           <div class="fi-module-player__content">
            <span class="fi-module-player__content__navigation-title hidden">
             SIX
            </span>
            <p class="fi-module-player__content__caption">
             GUINEA
            </p>
            <h2 class="fi-module-player__content__title">
             "Reaching Qatar 2022 was added as a clause in my contract"
            </h2>
            <div class="fi-module-player__content__text fi-module-player__content__long">
             <p>
              Guinea’s youth teams have competed on the world stage on multiple occasions, participating at the FIFA U-20 World Cup twice (Japan 1979 and Korea Republic 2017) and no fewer than four editions of the FIFA U-17 World Cup.
             </p>
             <p>
              One factor that has contributed to the country’s successful national youth teams is the exceptional football academies located in the capital, Conakry. Even when the country grappled with an Ebola outbreak between 2014 and 2015, their U-17 and U-20 teams made the World Cup. So why have the senior team never managed to qualify for the global showpiece?
             </p>
             <p>
              <strong>
               FIFA.com
              </strong>
              spoke with Guinea’s French coach Didier Six, who enjoyed a notable playing career with French, English, Turkish and German clubs and was part of a wonderful France team that dazzled on the world stage and won UEFA EURO 1984.
             </p>
             <p>
              In charge of Guinea since 2019, his goal - as he explains in this interview - is to lead the country to their maiden appearance at the FIFA World Cup™.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="fi-module-player__content__text fi-module-player__content__short">
             <p>
              Guinea’s youth teams have competed on the world stage on multiple occasions, participating at the FIFA U-20 World Cup twice and no fewer than four editions of the FIFA U-17 World Cup.
             </p>
             <p>
              So why have the senior team never managed to qualify for the global showpiece?
             </p>
             <p>
              <strong>
               FIFA.com
              </strong>
              spoke with Guinea’s French coach Didier Six, who enjoyed a notable playing career with French, English, Turkish and German clubs and was part of a wonderful France team that dazzled on the world stage and won UEFA EURO 1984.
             </p>
             <p>
              In charge of Guinea since 2019, his goal - as he explains in this interview - is to lead the country to their maiden appearance at the FIFA World Cup™.
             </p>
            </div>
            <a class="btn btn-primary" href="https://www.fifa.com/worldcup/news/six-the-world-cup-is-the-dream-of-all-guineans">
             FULL INTERVIEW
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="col-sm-6 col-md-7">
           <div class="fi-module-player__image fi-o-media-object__teaser">
            <img alt="Didier Six." class="lazyload BLABLA" data-src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_l4/v1615887197/mrsytceuixnaql23siym.jpg" src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_l4/t_lazy/v1615887197/mrsytceuixnaql23siym.jpg"/>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="row">
          <div class="col-md-7 pull-right">
           <div class="fi-module-player__quote">
            <svg class="fi-svg-icon icon-quote">
             <use xlink:href="#icon-quote">
             </use>
            </svg>
            <div class="fi-promo__summary">
             <p>
              There’s a lot of potential in Africa and there’s been a major transformation in terms of mentality. Now, they must get over the idea that an African team can’t go beyond the World Cup quarter-finals.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>

          <symbol id="icon-quote" viewbox="0 0 44 30">
           <path d="M14.9873047,0.471191406 C10.7571403,2.05290504 7.31788434,4.35187294 4.66943359,7.36816406 C2.02098285,10.3844552 0.696777344,13.9892368 0.696777344,18.1826172 C0.696777344,21.2356923 1.67153973,23.8105364 3.62109375,25.9072266 C5.57064777,28.0039167 7.79604869,29.0522461 10.2973633,29.0522461 C12.0997811,29.0522461 13.755038,28.5004938 15.2631836,27.3969727 C16.7713292,26.2934515 17.5253906,24.7117616 17.5253906,22.6518555 C17.5253906,20.8126536 16.9000714,19.3872935 15.6494141,18.3757324 C14.3987568,17.3641714 13.16651,16.8583984 11.9526367,16.8583984 C11.290524,16.8583984 10.4628956,17.0239241 9.46972656,17.3549805 C8.80761388,17.6124687 8.27425333,17.7412109 7.86962891,17.7412109 C6.5086195,17.7412109 5.828125,16.6193146 5.828125,14.3754883 C5.828125,11.8741737 6.6373617,9.77751497 8.25585938,8.08544922 C9.87435705,6.39338347 12.1181497,4.71973484 14.9873047,3.06445312 L14.9873047,0.471191406 Z M41.4165039,0.471191406 C37.1863395,2.05290504 33.7470836,4.35187294 31.0986328,7.36816406 C28.4501821,10.3844552 27.1259766,13.9892368 27.1259766,18.1826172 C27.1259766,21.2356923 28.100739,23.8105364 30.050293,25.9072266 C31.999847,28.0039167 34.2252479,29.0522461 36.7265625,29.0522461 C38.5289804,29.0522461 40.1842373,28.5004938 41.6923828,27.3969727 C43.2005284,26.2934515 43.9545898,24.7117616 43.9545898,22.6518555 C43.9545898,20.8126536 43.3292706,19.3872935 42.0786133,18.3757324 C40.827956,17.3641714 39.5957092,16.8583984 38.3818359,16.8583984 C37.7197233,16.8583984 36.8920948,17.0239241 35.8989258,17.3549805 C35.2368131,17.6124687 34.7034525,17.7412109 34.2988281,17.7412109 C32.9378187,17.7412109 32.2573242,16.6193146 32.2573242,14.3754883 C32.2573242,11.8741737 33.0665609,9.77751497 34.6850586,8.08544922 C36.3035563,6.39338347 38.5473489,4.71973484 41.4165039,3.06445312 L41.4165039,0.471191406 Z">

        <div class="container-fluid">
         <div class="section__header">
          <div class="h1 section__title">
           Seleção coach talks top coaches and star players
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="fi-article-feature-bg__mask--nobrand">
         <div class="fi-module-player__bg">
          <picture>
           <!--[if IE 9]><video style="display: none;"><![endif]-->
           <source data-srcset="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_l1/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg" media="(min-width: 1200px)"/>
           <source data-srcset="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_tc1/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg" media="(min-width: 1024px)"/>
           <source data-srcset="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_l3/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg" media="(min-width: 768px)"/>
           <source data-srcset="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_p3/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg" media="(min-width: 320px)"/>
           <!--[if IE 9]></video><![endif]-->
           <img alt="Tite coach of Brazil gestures during a match between Brazil and Bolivia as part of South American Qualifiers for Qatar 2022 at Neo Quimica Arena on October 09, 2020 in Sao Paulo, Brazil." class="img-responsive lazyload" data-src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_p3/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg" onerror="setDefaultPicture(this,'t_l1', 't_tc1', 't_l3', 't_p3');" src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_tc1/t_lazy/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg"/>
          </picture>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="fi-article-feature-bg__mask--ie--nobrand">
         <div class="fi-module-player__bg">
          <picture>
           <img alt="Tite coach of Brazil gestures during a match between Brazil and Bolivia as part of South American Qualifiers for Qatar 2022 at Neo Quimica Arena on October 09, 2020 in Sao Paulo, Brazil." class="image-r image-responsive" src="https://img.fifa.com/image/upload/t_l1/v1614674345/lr4bckkg5sl4dfejedwe.jpg"/>
          </picture>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="container-fluid">
         <div class="row">
          <div class="col-sm-6 col-md-5">
           <div class="fi-module-player__content">
            <span class="fi-module-player__content__navigation-title hidden">
             TITE
            </span>
            <p class="fi-module-player__content__caption">
             BRAZIL
            </p>
            <h2 class="fi-module-player__content__title">
             "I without doubt learned the most from Ancelotti"
            </h2>
            <div class="fi-module-player__content__text fi-module-player__content__long">
             <p>
              “Surviving for long in a country that has 200 million Seleção coaches is impossible,” summarised Luiz Felipe Scolari of what many deem the most demanding job in football.
             </p>
             <p>
              Mario Zagallo was A Seleção’s eighth coach in the five years leading up to Mexico 1970. Carlos Alberto Parreira was their fourth appointment in little over a year in 1991. Scolari became the fourth in nine months ten years later. Only one man in history – Flavio Costa, who was in charge between 1944 and ’50 - has spent over five years in the canary-yellow chair.
             </p>
             <p>
              A man who is not only surviving, but thriving in the proverbial poisoned chalice in set to double that statistic. Tite has won 38 and lost just four of 52 matches. The 59-year-old has masterminded Brazil’s best-ever start to a World Cup qualifying campaign. And fundamentally in a land where, to many, futebol-arte is as paramount as three points, he’s keeping the insatiable satiated.
             </p>
             <p>
              Tite took time out from his hectic schedule – he watches and analyses matches with the regularity other Brazilians drink coffee – to chat to
              <strong>
               FIFA.com
              </strong>
              about the upcoming clashes with Colombia and Argentina, Diego Maradona, Neymar, Philippe Coutinho and Alisson, and why he took a year out from coaching to study the beautiful game.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="fi-module-player__content__text fi-module-player__content__short">
             <p>
              “Surviving for long in a country that has 200 million Seleção coaches is impossible,” summarised Luiz Felipe Scolari of what many deem the most demanding job in football.
             </p>
             <p>
              But although only one man in history – Flavio Costa, who was in charge between 1944 and ’50 - has spent over five years in the canary-yellow chair, a man who is not only surviving, but thriving with the proverbial poisoned chalice in set to double that statistic.
             </p>
             <p>
              Tite has won 38 and lost just four of 52 matches. The 59-year-old has masterminded Brazil’s best-ever start to a World Cup qualifying campaign. And fundamentally in a land where, to many, futebol-arte is as paramount as three points, he’s keeping the insatiable satiated.
             </p>
             <p>
              Tite took time out from his hectic schedule – he watches and analyses matches with the regularity other Brazilians drink coffee – to chat to
              <strong>
               FIFA.com
              </strong>
              about the upcoming clashes with Colombia and Argentina, Diego Maradona, Neymar, Philippe Coutinho and Alisson, and why he took a year out from coaching to study the beautiful game.
             </p>
            </div>
            <a class="btn btn-primary" href="https://www.fifa.com/worldcup/news/tite-neymar-has-become-a-bow-and-arrow">
             FULL INTERVIEW
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>

          <div class="col-sm-6 col-md-5">
           <div class="fi-module-player__content">
            <span class="fi-module-player__content__navigation-title hidden">
             MARTINEZ
            </span>
            <p class="fi-module-player__content__caption">
             BELGIUM
            </p>
            <h2 class="fi-module-player__content__title">
             "I don’t worry about the golden generation tag anymore"
            </h2>
            <div class="fi-module-player__content__text fi-module-player__content__long">
             <p>
              <em>
               “Don’t tell me what’s wrong. Tell me how you’d fix it.”
              </em>
             </p>
             <p>
              Roberto Martinez can see now that his life and career have been shaped by these words and the man who recited them. That challenge, to solve a problem identified on the pitch, came from his father, himself a player, coach and football obsessive. And it was posed, repeatedly, to Roberto from the age of just nine. Even now, as the 47-year-old coach and technical director of the world’s top-ranked team, he is still subjected to the same conversations-cum-interrogations from this most demanding of mentors.
             </p>
             <p>
              These days, he can of course bring to these animated father-son chats a wealth of evidence that underline his credentials as an elite coach and accomplished problem-solver.
             </p>
             <p>
              The most recent exhibits include leading Belgium to their best-ever finish at a FIFA World Cup™ and, for the past three years, keeping them perched imperiously at the summit of FIFA/Coca World Ranking. All that is left to do with the Red Devils is win a major trophy and, in this interview, the man leading their ‘golden generation’ tells
              <strong>
               FIFA.com
              </strong>
              how much he is savouring that challenge.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="fi-module-player__content__text fi-module-player__content__short">
             <p>
              <em>
               “Don’t tell me what’s wrong. Tell me how you’d fix it.”
              </em>
             </p>
             <p>
              Roberto Martinez can see now that his life and career have been shaped by these words and the man who recited them. That challenge, to solve a problem identified on the pitch, came from his father, himself a player, coach and football obsessive. And it was posed, repeatedly, to Roberto from the age of just nine. Even now, as the 47-year-old coach and technical director of the world’s top-ranked team, he is still subjected to the same conversations-cum-interrogations from this most demanding of mentors.
             </p>
             <p>
              These days, he can of course bring to these animated father-son chats a wealth of evidence that underline his credentials as an elite coach and accomplished problem-solver.
             </p>
             <p>
              The most recent exhibits include leading Belgium to their best-ever finish at a FIFA World Cup™ and, for the past three years, keeping them perched imperiously at the summit of FIFA/Coca World Ranking. All that is left to do with the Red Devils is win a major trophy and, in this interview, the man leading their ‘golden generation’ tells
              <strong>
               FIFA.com
              </strong>
              how much he is savouring that challenge.
             </p>
            </div>

    <script type="text/javascript">
     var RankingHP = {
    init: function () {
      if ($('div').fi_select === undefined) {
        console.log('FF fi_select undefined');
        setTimeout(RankingHP.init, 2000);      
        return;
      }
      $('.fi-select-wrapper.fi-select__ranking').fi_select();
      $(".fifa-ranking-section__nav a").on("click", function () {
        var _id = $(this).parent().data("value");
        RankingHP.setRankingModuleVisibility(_id);
      });
      $("select.fifa-ranking-section__nav").on("change", function () {
        var _id = $(this).val();
        RankingHP.setRankingModuleVisibility(_id);
      });
    },
    setRankingModuleVisibility: function (id) {
      $('.fifa-ranking-section__content').removeClass('fi-module-ranking__content--active');
      $('.fi-Ranking__logo').removeClass('hidden');
      $('#' + id).addClass('fi-module-ranking__content--active');
      $('.fi-Ranking__logo:not([data-attr="' + id + '"])').addClass('hidden');
    }
  }

  $(document).ready(function () {
    RankingHP.init();
  });
    </script>

           <h3 class="d3-o-media-object__title fancy-gallery-overlay-caption__title">
            Hallowed Turf: Rose Bowl
           </h3>
           <p class="d3-o-media-object__date fancy-gallery-overlay-caption__date">
            Tuesday, 12 Jan 2021
           </p>
           <p class="d3-o-media-object__summary">
            In Pasadena, USA lies an iconic colosseum famous for a wealth of sporting history. During the 90s, it played host to two monumental tournaments, witnessing two epic penalty shoot-outs in the finals of both the FIFA World Cup™ and the FIFA Women’s World Cup™. This is: the Rose Bowl.

From Brazil lifting their fourth FIFA World Cup Trophy in 1994 to Brandi Chastain's iconic penalty and celebration for the USA against China PR in 1999, the Rose Bowl has been the setting of many historic moments.

            Hallowed Turf: Estadio Azteca
           </h3>
           <p class="d3-o-media-object__date fancy-gallery-overlay-caption__date">
            Tuesday, 05 Jan 2021
           </p>
           <p class="d3-o-media-object__summary">
            When it comes to iconic football stadiums, it is impossible not to mention one distinct ground in Mexico City. A temple steeped in FIFA World Cup history, it was the setting for two finals that saw both Pele and Diego Maradona lifting the Trophy. This is the Estadio Azteca.

From the Game of the Century featuring Italy and West Germany to Maradona’s handball and sublime solo goal for Argentina against England, the Estadio Azetca has been the setting for unforgettable World Cup moments.
